The┬аOriya┬аJagmohana/Jaganmohana┬аR─Бm─Бyaс╣Зa(early 16th┬аcentury,
also called as the┬аD__─Б__с╣Зс╕Н__i┬аR__─Б__m__─Б__ya__с╣З__a┬аafter the meter used
in its composition) by the great Oriya┬а┼Ы┼л__dramuni┬аBaс╕╖r─Бmad─Бsa, the most renowned of the legendary┬аpancasakh__─Б┬аpoets of Oriya literature, has perhaps the earliest
reference in the Eastern┬аR__─Б__m__─Б__ya__с╣З__a┬аtradition of the motif of┬а┼Ъabar─лтАЩs feeding R─Бma┬аucchi__с╣гс╣н__a┬аfruits, though the
fruits are mangoes and not jujubes. This is certainly the most fetching version
of this motif. This massive┬аR__─Б__m__─Б__ya__с╣З__a┬а(it is many times the size of the┬аV__─Б__lm__─л__ki R__─Б__m__─Б__ya__с╣З__a) has been transliterated
into┬аn__─Б__gar__─л┬аcharacters and translated into Hindi (Jagmohana┬аR__─Б__m__─Б__ya__с╣З__a┬а[D__─Б__с╣Зс╕Нi┬аR__─Б__m__─Б__yaс╣Зa],┬аs__─Б__nuvad Devn__─Б__gar__─л_┬аlipyantaraс╣З. Kartt__─Б__: Yoge__┼Ы__var Trip__─Б__с╣нhi тАЬYog__─л__.тАЭ_┬аLakhnau: Bhuvan V__─Б__с╣З__─л_┬ас╣мrasс╣н_, 1991, 5 volumes). In
this retelling, after the┬аKabandhavadha, the brothers encounter
a┬а┼Ъabara┬аand a ┼Ъabar─л on
the way. The┬а┼Ъabara asks R─Бma his name and lineage and after being
informed in short the narrative up to this point, the┬а┼Ъabaraс╣З─л,
i.e.,┬а┼Ъabar─л venerates the brothers and takes them to her hermitage and
tells R─Бma that she was waiting for his arrival, which was foretold to her by
Indra. She tells him that she has saved the choicest fruits and roots for him
and upon beholding the fruits and roots which all bore teeth-marks, R─Бma
praises her for saving the best and the sweetest for him and devours them
vigorously. In a lovely narration,┬а┼Ъabar─л offers R─Бma an unbitten┬аsundar─л┬аmango,
which R─Бma instead of eating throws on the ground, stating that since it was
тАЬunmarkedтАЭ (amudr─Б) by her teeth, he had no way of knowing that it was
sweet and if it was, she ought to have marked it with her teeth! Baс╕╖r─Бmad─Бsa
states that when┬а┼Ъabar─л received the foretelling of R─БmaтАЩs arrival, she
entered a mango-grove and started gathering mangoes, verifying that they were
sweet and not sour by biting them. R─Бma here states that he will not consume
untasted fruits and insists that the fruits be tasted before he consumes them!
The┬аJagmohan┬аR─Бm─Бyaс╣Зa┬аhas a polemical backdrop,
being the first religious text composed in Oriya, prior to which only Sanskrit
could enter the temples, due to which it is believed that Baс╕╖r─Бmad─Бsa composed
this text on the balustrade (jaganmohana┬аin Oriya) outside the
famous Jagann─Бtha temple. W.L. Smith in his lovely study (R─Бm─Бyaс╣Зa
Traditions in Eastern India:┬аAssam, Bengal, Orissa. Department
of Indology, University of Stockholm: Stockholm, 1988) refers briefly to this
episode at┬аpage 125:

The terse┬аBrajbh─Бс╣г─Б┬аBhaktam─Бl
of N─Бbh─Бd─Бs┬а(ca. 1624), a highly-condensed тАЬrosaryтАЭ

twenty-three┬а_bhakta_s who are termed тАЬbeloved of the LordтАЭ (Harivallabh)

out in┬а**ca. 1712┬а**by one┬аPriy─Бd─Бs, who composed an elaborate

(┼Ъabar─л) and generate a considerable┬аbhakti┬атАЬback-storyтАЭ for
her (_Gosv─Бmi ┼Ъr─лn─Бbh─Бji krt Bhaktam─Бl. ┼Ъr─л Priy─Бd─Бsj─л praс╣Зit┬ас╣м─лk─Б-Kavitt
┼Ъr─л Ayodhy─Бniv─Бs─л ┼Ъr─л S─лt─Бr─Бm┼Ыaraс╣З┬аBhagv─Бnpras─Бd R┼лpakal─Б┬аviracit

Towards the end of
the┬а18th┬аcentury, the Bengali poet Jagadr─Бma wrote
a┬аR─Бm─Бyaс╣Зa (known as the R─Бmpras─Бd─л-Jagadr─Бm─л┬аR─Бm─Бyaс╣Зa,
since the poet is handed over the poem after the┬аLank─Бk─Бс╣Зс╕Нa┬аto
his son R─Бmpras─Бd, who continued and completed the work) intending, like
earlier Bengali poets, to harmonize┬аVaiс╣гс╣Зava┬аand┬а┼Ъ─Бkta┬аideas
by combining the Sanskrit┬аAdbhutaR─Бm─Бyaс╣Зa┬аand
the┬аAdhy─БtmaR─Бm─Бyaс╣Зa. This work, alas, does not appear
to be have been translated or transliterated. In this work R─Бma, conscious and
concerned that his every action will be liable to be judged and evaluated by
his devotees, is extremely cautious in all his acts. Thus, when
┼Ъabar─л┬аoffers him fruit which she has first tasted, he thinks тАЬIf I feel
disgust and do not eat this fruit, my name as one who is obligated to his
devotees will be gone at once. Therefore, I must eat the leavings of
┼Ъabar─л.тАЭ┬аSmith┬аrefers to this episode at┬аpage 111┬аof
his book:
